Hello,  
  
This works fine even in a very narrow ranging periods. If lets say you highest time frame you want to trade is H4. Then you will have to follow the slope on that chart. If the price is very ranging you will not get the same slope on H1 and H30 at the same time. This means no trade. However, its not a perfect system, and i've not seen one yet. Works good for me almost 85% winning ratio.   
  
EMATRADER

Hello,  
  
I did not came up with this system. My friend who is trading Forex since 5 years showed me how he trades. I've been trading with this system with just over 6 months. 85% means 85 winning trades from 100. Should i show you my statement? Sorry i won't. Anyways, i'm not selling this system. Try it for your self. It is based no nothing but trend. You decied which highest time frame you want to trade (depend on for how long you want to hold your trade). Then simply follow its slope and to find the best entry use lower time frame. Most false signals will be eliminated by looking at lower time frame slope. If lower time frames are moving in opposite direction we don't enter the trade. You should have a good knowledge of money management if you don't want to loose money even if your win ratio is 99%![](https://resources.faireconomy.media/images/emojis/64/1f609.png?v=15.1).  
Anyways try it on a demo. You have nothing to loose.  
  
Cheers.  
EMATRADER

Hello,  
  
Yes you are right. But its depend which time frame you want to trade. I trade mostly from H4 and daily cuz i have day job. For for you if you want to trade from H4 chart. Lets says on H4 you just saw downtred. Then you have to wait for best entry point. Wait untill H1 and M30 have turn down along with H4. If you want to trade from 30M chart. Comfirm it by looking at 15M and 5M charts just like for H4 charts.  
  
EMATRADER

  * [#20](/thread/post/1657640#post1657640 "Post Permalink")

  * Edited 12:24am  Oct 21, 2007 12:22am | Edited 12:24am 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar18341_4.gif) alcastro](alcastro)

  * | Joined Sep 2006  | Status: Pipchaser | [512 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=18341)

HI,  
  
I like the simplicity of your long trade system. I also have a day time job and therefore have to limit myself to the dailies.  
I was doing a quick backtest on your system and noticed that many times, if you wait until the slope line flattens, after you have entered a trade, you may end up giving many pips, or even losing some. Have you considered using trailing stops? in that way you may lock some pips as you follow the trend and get out either when the slope line flattens or when you get stopped out.  
Which pairs do you usually trade? Which have proved to work best based in your experience?  
  
I am waiting for your short term system too. Might be good to grab some pips during the small periods of time when I am in front of the computer.

Hi,  
As i was told to trade 4 major pairs i only trade EUR/USD,GBP/USD,USD/JPY,USD/CHF. All of them works good. I tried once GBP/JPY and stop lose of 100 was hit. I never tried again anyother pair.   
I don't use trailing stop. I ajust my SL/TP everyday. Yes you will loose some profit. But again, if you know more about pair you are trading you can use trailing stop. Or even close your position after you have gain a nice profit rather then waitng for the slope to go flat. For example, if you are happy with 300 PIP profit close your position even if the slope is still showing down trend. You know what i mean.  
  
Or enter more then one lot. Exit one by one when you desire TP hit. I mean you would need a good money mangement knowledge otherwise this system might not help.  
  
Thanks  
EMATRADER

>  Yes you are right. But its depend which time frame you want to trade. I trade mostly from H4 and daily cuz i have day job. For for you if you want to trade from H4 chart. Lets says on H4 you just saw downtred. Then you have to wait for best entry point. Wait untill H1 and M30 have turn down along with H4. If you want to trade from 30M chart. Comfirm it by looking at 15M and 5M charts just like for H4 charts.  
>    
>  EMATRADER

Hello,  
  
I don't enter in a new trade if there will be a major news release i'll wait till the news impact is over. However if i'm in a trade already from few days i won't close it i'll simply move my stop loss very close about 10min before the major news release. So incase the news goes in the favour of my trade i'll gain some extra pip in no time. When the pair is in a range ... lets say you want to trade from the daily chart. If you see a new downtrend on it but the pair is in range. 85% of the time you will not have the same slope on H4,H1 and 30M they will move in the opposite direction. However, few times they will not and you might loose that trade which is about 15% of the time.  
Hope this help. Looking forward for your demo results.  
  
Thanks  
EMATRADER

  * [#31](/thread/post/1667158#post1667158 "Post Permalink")

  * Oct 21, 2007 7:39am  Oct 21, 2007 7:39am 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar11336_4.gif) Trader_V](trader_v)

  * | Joined Jun 2006  | Status: Patience, Discipline & Desire!!! | [291 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=11336)

Man I will tell you what... You could not have posted this indicator and your method for trading it at a more perfect time for me than now. I have been reading the 25-50 thread by Effi Lang. Nice somplistic system. I think I would adapt a few things from it and may even demo tha system using this trading methodology using multiple TF's but that's another story ![](https://resources.faireconomy.media/images/emojis/64/1f609.png?v=15.1)  
  
OK so getting back to timing. I have been trying to find a way yo get m trading system down to a "SYSTEM" (you really new traders should read that again ![](https://resources.faireconomy.media/images/emojis/64/1f60a.png?v=15.1)) but I just could not solidify my rules. Now with this methodology I can finally do it ![](https://resources.faireconomy.media/images/emojis/64/1f601.png?v=15.1)  
  
Now look we all know there is no holy grail. So again you new folks reading this, understand this one concept "the most successful traders had mre lsing trades than winning trades" the only difference between them and us is they came to the market to reamin there for a long time and they no how to cut there losses and le the winners run.  
  
Now what ematrader has shown everyone here is not magic. Hell it's not even new, not by a long shot! This is the same methodology that has been used and dictated for years.  
  
Ask yourself this question:  
  
When trading a market that trends better than anything else out there, WHY WOULD YOU TRADE AGAINST IT???!!!  
  
This system is an easy to follow trend following system that let's you capitalize on market moves by determining the trend with a higher TF and timing your entry with the lower TF's. This helps prevent (not always) gettign caught in an intra-trend move. In other words if the dominant trend is down it will help prevent entering in a short position while the market is retracing.  
  
I think a few things could be done to help optimize this system for others.   
  
For example one thing to help more conservative traders is to (as ematrader said) identify areas of S/R if you are looking to enter the market short based on the primary daily trend (entry based on 1H charts) You would look for price action setups entering trades using stop orders on breakouts. Check the chart in the next post for an example.  
  
I have a few other thoughts as well and will post when time permits but wanted to put my thanks out there to ematrader for sharing this system and to those of you who will help to optimize this.  
  
Additionally I as well as ematrader (I assume) would not like to see this system transformed into something unrecognizable as this thread develops. Optimizations from this point should remain about entry exit and money management IMHO.  
  
Ok my fingers are really tired now...lol

I know he has been trading for 5 years and showed you this system, but does he work for a brokerage, how did he come about this system? That kind of stuff. A little history about a systems origins is always an interesting little story.  
  
OK I'm really done now...lol

  * [#33](/thread/post/1667165#post1667165 "Post Permalink")

  * Oct 21, 2007 7:58am  Oct 21, 2007 7:58am 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar11336_4.gif) Trader_V](trader_v)

  * | Joined Jun 2006  | Status: Patience, Discipline & Desire!!! | [291 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=11336)

OK here is the example I spoke of in my last post.  
  
This is the GBP/JPY pair. I am showing the 1H TF. The UP ARROW on the left side indicates the bar on the 4H charts when the D1 and 4H agreed. The 1H agreed a few bars befor that.   
  
The second arrow indicates when the D1 changed. So looking for an entry on the 1H instead of placing a market order just to get in the market. We can help our selves by letting the market prove to us the trand is valid.  
  
You can see the market pulled back slightly just before it made a nice move down. Notice the bars in the black area inside the greenish square. You will see the end of the pullback (last bullish bar)followed by am inside bearish bar. Now it is perfect acceptable to enter on a break of that bar short. But I am a little more conservative than that and like the market to prove itself. So take notice of the next bar. It is a nice long bearish bar, indicating the move may be on and the intra-trend that I spoke about in my previous post is over. So O place a Sell Stop order at 243.00. This is about 20 pips beloe the low of that bar. You can see the next bar entered me into the trade.   
  
Ok great so now what? Well I like to add to my winners so as long as the trend is still intact (and it is) I look to see if there might be another opportunity to enter an additional order.   
  
Notice where that low area is just in front of that previous pullback. That is an area of support. So again the market makes a small retrace based on that previous area of support now forming a double bottom. So I place another sell stop about 20 pips below the low point of that support area. And what do you know I an entered again. But entered by allowing the market to prove itself.  
  
This is not a full post about trade management. But I wanted to show some alternatives to entering these longer term trades based on some price action.  
  
Hope this helps someone. In another post I may share how I woluld manage my stops and possibly another entry idea.  
  
EMATRADER.... Sorry man I am not trying to hijack your thread. I swear I'm not. I just got on this roll of typing this evening. Now I really gotta stop and go do something else for a while...lol  
  
OK I'm off for a little while at least

[Looking for the slope of a slope histogram?](/thread/811943-looking-for-the-slope-of-a-slope-histogram "i hope I make sense. Does anybody know of an indicator that will do the slope of a slope. I would like to have a slope histogram \(hma for...") 0 replies

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar49728_6.gif) darko80](darko80)

  * | Joined Sep 2007  | Status: Cyrox Active Trader | [75 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=49728)

done 80 pips on gbp/jpy (intraday method) in 10mins.  
I'm not surprised, cause as i said MTTF systems are the win in Forex ![](https://resources.faireconomy.media/images/emojis/64/1f609.png?v=15.1)  
and ematrader offers us a clear and simple tool to do it.  
  
On long time method use trailing stops, it's better. But remember to entry when all tf's have the same color (after 2 or 3 candles) and don't care about spikes...if it hit your s/l re-enter when all have the same color again  
  
Trend and Time are your friends.

Hey Darko,  
  
If you looking inside the indicator you will find that it it is not a straight moving average. It is instead a moving average of the moving average.  
  
So the slope is an oscillator not a MA.   
  
Enjoy  
Ademac  
  
**P.S Been looking into it further and it it is actually based on a HULL Trend.

My 2 pips observation and suggestion for those holding positions for a long period of time. It seems to me that is much safer and more logical to wait for the change in slope of directional line and get in in the beginning of the trend not just in the middle or when the bullish or bearish power is coming to an end. It's like taking a moving bus or a bus at stop.   
So from my posint of view I would take long eur/usd trade on Sep 11 at about 16.00 GMT+2 time. Daily slope just change to uptrend and all other TF's pointing up at that moment. Also we passed through strong resistance and round number. One can hold this position for one month for now and it's about 400 pips up. Not so bad if to consider one single trade and watching only 1 pair.   
Just imo..  
  
Thanks ematrader for posting this system.   
  
Best regards,  
TheThing

Good enough ristab, but if you want to make it better, you can use this way :  
  
In your MT4, you can click the "File" button on the left corner of your chart, then choose "save as picture", then choose "active chart" then "OK". Then you can save the picture to the folder where you want.   
And When you want to post reply, above the message box there's an "attachment" button, just click it, then upload your saved picture from your folder. After it finished, click again the "attachment" button. Then that's all, your picture has been attached.  
  
The second way, you can upload your picture to [tinypic](http://tinypic.com/), then there are several choices appear, you can choose this one **"IMG Code for Forums & Message Boards:**" and click the "copy" button, then paste it in your message box when you post a reply.   
I guess that's all, hopes this way can help you.  
  
Regards,  
  
IIN

  * [#85](/thread/post/1762625#post1762625 "Post Permalink")

  * Dec 17, 2007 6:35pm  Dec 17, 2007 6:35pm 

  * [ Lenoxer](lenoxer)

  * | Joined Nov 2007  | Status: Live long and prosper | [359 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=54983)

Dear Slope Thread,  
  
I've yet to do any testing whatsoever on this system but as a hedge fund manager used to great and costly amounts of trader error and the unending, all-too-rough approximations that pass for our judgments on market direction, I am impressed with the "good enough" aspects of this method: the jibing of multiple timeframes (which seems to me de rigeur with respect to technical trading) in a purely binary fashion: if the timeframes lines are red it's short; if white you're long. Put in your 100 point stop. Hang in there. As Einstein said, everything should be as simple as possible but no simpler. But, I do have one pesky question: does the slope system really work?  
  
My best to everyone,  
  
Lenoxer

  * [#126](/thread/post/1774025#post1774025 "Post Permalink")

  * Dec 27, 2007 8:53pm  Dec 27, 2007 8:53pm 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar27318_4.gif) Freewheelin](freewheelin)

  * | Joined Dec 2006  | Status: a german in greece | [128 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=27318)

I followed this thread from the beginning and have a question about the entries and the logic behind them.  
  
Let's say we want to trade off the 5min chart. What I found is that the higher timeframes are not behaving independently from the lower. Attached chart shows 5min, 15min, 30min and 60min.  
As you can see the slope line changes color in lower timeframes: first 5min, then 15min and so forth. The highest TF is the last.  
This is clear to me, because the higher TF includes the action in the lower ones.  
But:  
If you entry by the time the highest TF changes color it is NOT trading off a lower TF like 5min, because most of the times they are already blue (like in the attached chart) - it is trading from the HIGHER TF.   
There is no such thing like timing the entry - you are only trading the chosen high TF.  
  
Does it make sense to you? Hope so...  
Would it make much more sense to wait for the slope changing its color to the opposite? And to enter after the next change? For example: All TF line up blue - we wait the lowest TF slope change to red and enter after the next change to blue. Like a retracement.  
  
Look at the chart (60min still in progress, but i believe it'll stay blue)

> [Quoting Lenoxer](/thread/post/1773812#post1773812 "View Quoted Post")
> 
> Disliked
> 
> Dear Thread,   
>    
>  Is there any expert out there who can post the   
>  TEXT contained within the ex4 file of the slope indicator? I am trying to pay to have this indicator coded up for eSignal and am happy to share the result with everyone afterwards.  
>    
>  Thanks,  
>    
>  Lenoxer
> 
> Ignored

Here it is -   
  
//+------------------------------------------------------------------+   
//| HMA.mq4   
//| Copyright ![](https://resources.faireconomy.media/images/emojis/64/00a9-fe0f.png?v=15.1) 2006 WizardSerg <wizardserg@mail.ru>, ?? ??????? ForexMagazine #104   
//| [wizardserg@mail.ru](mailto:wizardserg@mail.ru)   
//| Revised by IgorAD,igorad2003@yahoo.co.uk |   
//| Personalized by iGoR AKA FXiGoR for the Trend Slope Trading method (T_S_T)   
//| Link:   
//| contact: [thefuturemaster@hotmail.com](mailto:thefuturemaster@hotmail.com)   
//+------------------------------------------------------------------+  
#property copyright "MT4 release WizardSerg <wizardserg@mail.ru>, ?? ??????? ForexMagazine #104"   
#property link "wizardserg@mail.ru"   
  
#property indicator_chart_window   
#property indicator_buffers 3   
#property indicator_color2 Blue   
#property indicator_color3 Red   
#property indicator_color1 Orange   
#property indicator_width1 1  
#property indicator_width2 1  
#property indicator_width3 1  
  
//---- input parameters   
extern int period=20;   
extern int method=3; // MODE_LWMA   
extern int price=0; // PRICE_CLOSE  
extern int EmailON=1; // 0 = false 1 = true  
extern int SoundON=1; // 0 = false 1 = true  
//---- buffers   
double Uptrend[];  
double Dntrend[];  
double ExtMapBuffer[];   
double buff[];  
  
  
//+------------------------------------------------------------------+   
//| Custom indicator initialization function |   
//+------------------------------------------------------------------+   
int init()   
{   
IndicatorBuffers(3);   
SetIndexBuffer(1, Uptrend);   
//ArraySetAsSeries(Uptrend, true);   
SetIndexBuffer(2, Dntrend);   
//ArraySetAsSeries(Dntrend, true);   
//SetIndexBuffer(2, ExtMapBuffer);   
//ArraySetAsSeries(Uptrend, true);  
SetIndexBuffer(0, ExtMapBuffer);   
ArraySetAsSeries(ExtMapBuffer, true);   
  
SetIndexStyle(0,DRAW_LINE);  
SetIndexStyle(1,DRAW_LINE);  
SetIndexStyle(2,DRAW_LINE);  
  
IndicatorShortName("Slope Direction Line("+period+")");   
return(0);   
}   
  
//+------------------------------------------------------------------+   
//| Custor indicator deinitialization function |   
//+------------------------------------------------------------------+   
int deinit()   
{   
// ???? ????? ?????? ??????   
return(0);   
}   
  
//+------------------------------------------------------------------+   
//| ?????????? ??????? |   
//+------------------------------------------------------------------+   
double WMA(int x, int p)   
{   
return(iMA(NULL, 0, p, 0, method, price, x));   
}   
  
//+------------------------------------------------------------------+   
//| Custom indicator iteration function |   
//+------------------------------------------------------------------+   
int start()   
{   
int counted_bars = IndicatorCounted();   
  
if(counted_bars < 0)   
return(-1);   
  
int x = 0;   
int p = MathSqrt(period);   
int e = Bars - counted_bars + period + 1;   
  
double vect[], trend[];   
  
if(e > Bars)   
e = Bars;   
  
ArrayResize(vect, e);   
ArraySetAsSeries(vect, true);  
ArrayResize(trend, e);   
ArraySetAsSeries(trend, true);   
  
for(x = 0; x < e; x++)   
{   
vect[x] = 2*WMA(x, period/2) - WMA(x, period);   
// Print("Bar date/time: ", TimeToStr(Time[x]), " close: ", Close[x], " vect[", x, "] = ", vect[x], " 2*WMA(p/2) = ", 2*WMA(x, period/2), " WMA(p) = ", WMA(x, period));   
}   
  
for(x = 0; x < e-period; x++)  
  
ExtMapBuffer[x] = iMAOnArray(vect, 0, p, 0, method, x);   
  
for(x = e-period; x >= 0; x--)  
{   
trend[x] = trend[x+1];  
if (ExtMapBuffer[x]> ExtMapBuffer[x+1]) trend[x] =1;  
if (ExtMapBuffer[x]< ExtMapBuffer[x+1]) trend[x] =-1;  
  
if (trend[x]>0)  
{ Uptrend[x] = ExtMapBuffer[x];   
if (trend[x+1]<0) Uptrend[x+1]=ExtMapBuffer[x+1];  
Dntrend[x] = EMPTY_VALUE;  
}  
else   
if (trend[x]<0)  
{   
Dntrend[x] = ExtMapBuffer[x];   
if (trend[x+1]>0) Dntrend[x+1]=ExtMapBuffer[x+1];  
Uptrend[x] = EMPTY_VALUE;  
}   
buff[x] = trend[x];   
  
//Print( " trend=",trend[x]);  
}  
if (EmailON==1 && Dntrend[0] != EMPTY_VALUE && Dntrend[1] == EMPTY_VALUE && isNewBar())  
{   
if (SoundON==1) Alert("SELL signal at Ask=",Ask,", Bid=",Bid,", Date=",TimeToStr(CurTime(),TIME_DATE)," ",TimeHour(CurTime()),":",TimeMinute(CurTime())," Symbol=",Symbol()," Period=",Period());  
SendMail("SELL signal alert","SELL signal at Ask="+DoubleToStr(Ask,4)+", Bid="+DoubleToStr(Bid,4)+", Date="+TimeToStr(CurTime(),TIME_DATE)+" "+TimeHour(CurTime())+":"+TimeMinute(CurTime())+" Symbol="+Symbol()+" Period="+Period());  
}  
if (EmailON==1 && Uptrend[0] != EMPTY_VALUE && Uptrend[1] == EMPTY_VALUE && isNewBar())   
{   
if (SoundON==1) Alert("BUY signal at Ask=",Ask,", Bid=",Bid,", Time=",TimeToStr(CurTime(),TIME_DATE)," ",TimeHour(CurTime()),":",TimeMinute(CurTime())," Symbol=",Symbol()," Period=",Period());  
SendMail("BUY signal alert","BUY signal at Ask="+DoubleToStr(Ask,4)+", Bid="+DoubleToStr(Bid,4)+", Date="+TimeToStr(CurTime(),TIME_DATE)+" "+TimeHour(CurTime())+":"+TimeMinute(CurTime())+" Symbol="+Symbol()+" Period="+Period());  
}  
return(0);   
}  
  
bool isNewBar()  
{  
static datetime lastbar=0;  
datetime curbar = Time[0];  
if(lastbar!=curbar)  
{  
lastbar=curbar;  
return (true);  
}  
else  
{  
return(false);  
}  
}   
  
  
//+------------------------------------------------------------------+   
  
Send me a copy when you are finished. I would greatly appreciate it.  
  
COTtrader  
"Ken" 

Decisions Determine Destiny -

posted on 7-9-2004 at 03:30 AM [](http://www.stockmeetingplace.com/forum/post.php?action=edit&fid=9&tid=8&pid=154)[http://www.stockmeetingplace.com/for...ilver/edit.gif](http://www.stockmeetingplace.com/forum/images/xpsilver/edit.gif) [](http://www.stockmeetingplace.com/forum/post.php?action=reply&fid=9&tid=8&repquote=154)[http://www.stockmeetingplace.com/for...lver/quote.gif](http://www.stockmeetingplace.com/forum/images/xpsilver/quote.gif)   
  
HMA Construction...  
The HMA is not that closely related to linear regression - the square root of the sum of the squares, etc. It is designed along geometric lines to remove lag without having to shorten the period and compromise smoothing. Hence, when compared to a line of linear regression of the same period, the HMA has superior smoothing.  
  
HMA Application...  
Because the HMA was designed to remove lag, don't use it to generate crossover trading signals. Instead you trade the turning points of the HMA...as it turns up - buy and as it turns down - sell. I actually prefer to use 2 separate HMAs with different periods - one for entry and one for exit. Tune the periods by backtesting on each financial instrument you wish to trade, ie. curve fit it in each case. Apply it to daily or weekly charts...it really doesn't matter which timeframe you use it over.  
  
Enjoy,  
Alan Hull   
  
  
  
I found this entry from the man himself, Alan Hull.

Dear Thread,  
  
What seems to me most attractive about the slope method is the ability to radically control trader error, otherwise known in the business world as quality control. If the lines are red, I'm short; white, I'm long. Such binary decision making combined with a large, unleveraged stop to adjust for the market's imprecision which in turn combined with $ volatility adjustments as per Aleksey's thread which in turn combined with several accounts using various Hull slope parameter settings to further adjust for the market's imprecisions just might do the trick.   
  
Lenoxer

  * Jan 1, 2008 7:38am  Jan 1, 2008 7:38am 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar43541_7.gif) Ronald Raygun](ronald*raygun)

  * Joined Jul 2007 | Status: 33 y/o Investor/Trader/Programmer | [5,016 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=43541)

I went through this system manually and it seems to be another winner in my book.   
  
I coded an EA based on my interpretation of the system itself. It incorporates the three timeframes into one chart.   
  
NOTE: You need my version of the trend slope line in the "indicator" folder.   
  
The variables are as follows:  
  
  
TrendSlopePeriod = Which MA to use. (80 is standard, 30 is debatable)  
BaseChartTF = The timeframe (In minutes) of your base chart.   
SecondaryChart = The timeframe (In minutes) of your secondary chart.   
TertiaryChart = The timeframe (In minutes) of your tertiary chart.   
  
  
The way this Ea works is that it enters with the standard buy setup, and exits with the opposite setup. This is a complete stop-and-reverse EA.   

Attached File(s)

![File Type: mq4](https://assets.faireconomy.media/images/attach/mq4.gif) [TrendSlope.mq4](/attachment/file/75484?d=1199140708) 11 KB | 1,817 downloads 

![File Type: mq4](https://assets.faireconomy.media/images/attach/mq4.gif) [Slope Direction Line.mq4](/attachment/file/75485?d=1199140708) 4 KB | 1,621 downloads

> Ignored

Yes, you have to put the minute equivalent for each field.   
  
1M =1  
5M =5  
15M =15  
30M =30  
1H = 60  
4H =240  
1D =1440  
1W (5 or 6 day week)=7200 or 8640  
etc.  
  

> [Quoting et_phonehome_2](/thread/post/1779340#post1779340 "View Quoted Post")
> 
> Disliked
> 
> Ronald  
>    
>  Can the EA be placed on any of the three timeframe charts?  
>    
>  Will the SlopeDirectionLine indicator still function correctly even if one does not use your EA?
> 
> Ignored

  
It doesn't matter which chart you place the EA on unless you change "EachTickMode" to false.   
  
When EachTickMode is false, that means that the EA will look for the entry point on the close of every bar in the timeframe the EA is in. For example, if you wanted your base chart to be 1 day, and you wanted the ea to check every 15 min for an entry point, you open a 15 min chart, enter the times necessary, set EachTickMode to false, and let it trade.   
  
The reason why I want you to use my version is because the EA is reading the data from it through the variables I listed. These variables are slightly different from the original. You can use the TrendSlope indicator on its own if you'd like. It's exactly the same thing.

  * [#156](/thread/post/1789570#post1789570 "Post Permalink")

  * Jan 8, 2008 1:08pm  Jan 8, 2008 1:08pm 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar43541_7.gif) Ronald Raygun](ronald*raygun)

  * Joined Jul 2007 | Status: 33 y/o Investor/Trader/Programmer | [5,016 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=43541)

Ok, I think I solved the logic issue.   
  
The Slope Direction Line indicator compares the current MA with the previous MA.   
  
If Current > Previous, slope is up  
If Current < Previous, slope is down  
  
Assuming that's the case, I set up the EA to look at the MA values of the three time frames, let's use the 1hr/30min/15min set.   
  
1HR Current > Previous  
30min Current > Previous  
15min Current > Previous  
  
If all of the above are true, then a buy signal. Otherwise, don't trade.   
  
1HR Current < Previous  
30min Current < Previous  
15min Current < Previous  
  
  
If all of the above are true, then a sell signal. Otherwise, don't trade.   
  
  
So far it is working well. I suggest that you don't use this on a tick-by-tick basis as there is repainting involved. You don't need the indicator anymore, it works on its own. The variables are the same.  
  
  
  
I have the EA setup on my server so that it checks the 1HR/30min/15min slope every 15 min. We'll see. No problems so far.

I would like to say that this system is a good one but I realized some difficulties when I was testing it. First of all, I use Long term strategy explained on the first page of this thread since I usually work and do not have enough time to monitor all my positions every 1 or 4 hours.I would like to say that I do not think it is necessary to use all 6 timeframes in order to open a trade. Small timeframes give a lot of false entries and most of time you just buy on local highs. I have been thinking about this problem and decided to make a Money managment for this system and a simple one is like you divide your trading size on 3 parts and first entry will be exactly when you get a signal following the strategy, a second entry is on 50 pips less if you want to buy and a third one is on the same level as the first trade.Generally a big problem with the system is when market is in a flat.

  * Jan 11, 2008 5:08pm  Jan 11, 2008 5:08pm 

  * [ COTtrader](cottrader)

  * | Joined Apr 2006  | Status: Trader | [62 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=8522)

Allvenis:  
  
If you are constrained by time then simply Trade the EA on a larger time frame chart. According to my understanding NO entries are made UNLESS the LARGEST time frame SIGNALS FIRST. In other words, an initial signal is given on the largest time frame and then each smaller TF is scoped UNTIL ALL the TFs agree THEN an ENTRY is made.   
  
COTtrader  
"Ken"

  * [ tjsun80](tjsun80)

Hello Allvenis,  
  
Based on this system, we do not actually use all 6 timeframes for entried.  
every entry is only based on the lower 2 timeframes.  
For example,if we would like to made an entry in daily chart, we only have to look at H4 and H1(or if you prefer look at M30 as well), this would be good enough for the entries.  
  
  

> [Quoting Allvenis](/thread/post/1794399#post1794399 "View Quoted Post")
> 
> Disliked
> 
> I would like to say that this system is a good one but I realized some difficulties when I was testing it. First of all, I use Long term strategy explained on the first page of this thread since I usually work and do not have enough time to monitor all my positions every 1 or 4 hours.I would like to say that I do not think it is necessary to use all 6 timeframes in order to open a trade. Small timeframes give a lot of false entries and most of time you just buy on local highs. I have been thinking about this problem and decided to make a Money managment for this system and a simple one is like you divide your trading size on 3 parts and first entry will be exactly when you get a signal following the strategy, a second entry is on 50 pips less if you want to buy and a third one is on the same level as the first trade.Generally a big problem with the system is when market is in a flat.
> 
> Ignored

  * Jan 15, 2008 1:34am  Jan 15, 2008 1:34am 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar43541_7.gif) Ronald Raygun](ronald*raygun)

  * Joined Jul 2007 | Status: 33 y/o Investor/Trader/Programmer | [5,016 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=43541)

Please list all your parameters. The EA checks them in a specific order.   
  
BaseTF first  
Secondard second   
Tertiary third   
  
So, your TFs should be  
  
240  
60  
30  
  
  
Also keep in mind that it only checks the current bar and previous bar to determine a trend. Looking at the candles, it looks like the Slope would have been negative at the time. 

[0 ](javascript:void\(0\);) [0 ](javascript:void\(0\);)

  * [ gfsound](gfsound)

  * | Joined Apr 2007  | Status: It's hard out there for a pip.... | [28 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=36476)

Wow, ok. It looks to me like the 4HR is most certainly an up slope, but obviously I'm wrong presuming the EA logic is working. Don't get me wrong; I'm not complaining as all trades are in profit, but I want to make sure I understand the logic. My parameters are as follows:  
  
MagicNumber=0  
SignalMail=0  
EachTickMode=1  
Lots=0.10000000  
Slippage=5  
UseStopLoss=1  
StopLoss=100  
UseTakeProfit=0  
TakeProfit=60  
UseTrailingStop=0  
TrailingStop=30  
MAPeriod=80  
BaseChart=240  
SecondaryChart=60  
TertiaryChart=30  
  
Again, it still looked to me as if the slope was heading up on the above chart posted (4HR), and as you can see it continued for several more candles blue/up before turning down (red).  
  
Lastly, will the EA exit positions upon a change in the slope? If so, which TF will it use? Or, should we have a specified TP based on Fibs, S/R, or some other methodology? So far I've just let the trades run and have not had the EA automatically close any positions, so just wondering. Thanks for your responses!

Hi guys,  
  
Seems like a good system here but beware, the slope indicator repaints.  
  
Just been watching it on the 1 min and it changed from green to red, (my colours) but is now showing all green again.  
  
This can generate false entries and make backtesting seem better than it is. However, if people make money from it and the EA works as specified it may not be an issue.  
  
G-Man

It did for me.

  * [#193](/thread/post/1806873#post1806873 "Post Permalink")

  * Jan 17, 2008 8:41pm  Jan 17, 2008 8:41pm 

  * [ Arctic4x](arctic4x)

  * | Joined Sep 2006  | Status: Trader | [213 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=18067)

Hi  
  
What you see is not really a repainting. It is some sort of graphical problem in MT4 i think.  
It is only the colour that changes but if you read the value of the indicator you see it stay the same so it is only a visual problem.  
I don't trade ea's but i am sure it should not make any problem for the ea because it only use the calculation of the value in the code and the colour does not matter i guess.  
I have used this indicator every day for 16 months and it do not repaint.  
Some time you can be a little bit fooled by the changing of the colour but it have never been a problem for me when i know about it.  
  
Arctic4x

  * [#195](/thread/post/1806922#post1806922 "Post Permalink")

  * Jan 17, 2008 9:04pm  Jan 17, 2008 9:04pm 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar43541_7.gif) Ronald Raygun](ronald*raygun)

  * Joined Jul 2007 | Status: 33 y/o Investor/Trader/Programmer | [5,016 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=43541)

The way that indicator works G-Man is that it looks at the current and previous MA values.   
  
What I think you saw was a current bar whose MA started out lower than the previous bar, but then went above it. The color change then was AT the previous bar which is what I think confused you. My EA works the same way. 

[0 ](javascript:void\(0\);) [0 ](javascript:void\(0\);)

No. G-Man is correct. I know it sounds very strange. I don't know programming and even if i did i would probably not be able to explain it but this is some sort of graphical problem in MT4.  
A person that knows programing and knows this indicator well explained to me that the problem is not in the indicator but in MT4.  
So because of that you can some times see that the colour between the two previous closed bars changes and show the wrong colour but the values are "correct"  
I know it probably sound impossible to a person that knows programing but like G-Man say if you run it some time on 1min chart you will probably see it.  
  
Arctic4x

  * Joined Jul 2007 | Status: 33 y/o Investor/Trader/Programmer | [5,016 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=43541)

Over my two-week testing, I went from $1,000 to about $1,200. A modest return I think, but it's a profit so I'm not complaining.  
  
EachTickMode means that for every trade that changes the price, the EA runs the calculations again to determine whether or not it should trade.   
  
When EachTickMode is false, then the EA checks at the close of the bar OF THE TIME FRAME IT IS POSTED IN. That's why I put my EA on the shortest time frame of my testing (15 mins in my case). It checks all three slopes every 15 mins which is reasonable because that's how often the slope can change. 

[0 ](javascript:void\(0\);) [0 ](javascript:void\(0\);)

Great system ematrader. ![](https://resources.faireconomy.media/images/emojis/64/1f44d.png?v=15.1)  
  
I've been playing around with a similar long term system using the daily chart, however I've not been using shorter timeframes for more accurate entry.  
I most certainly will consider it now.  
  
rgs

Depends. Trailing stop applies immediately. I set my trailing stop to 150 with I think a 100 pip initial stoploss.   
  
When the trade goes into 100 pips profit, the trailing stop takes over.

I'd have to agree with you. I've been banking pips and closing trades, but I've noticed the EA will just open them right back up in the same direction.  
  
I also agree with a previous post that it would be nice if the EA would close the trade if the lowest TF changed direction. This would take full advantage of MTF's, and preserve a good portion of the pips earned, instead of giving so many back. Also, it would allow us to test running this EA on several 3 TF sets to determine which might be most profitable.   
  
The last issue I'm still wondering about is I have eachtickmode set to false, which, according to Ronald:  
  
"When EachTickMode is false, then the EA checks at the close of the bar OF THE TIME FRAME IT IS POSTED IN."  
  
See attached chart of G/U on M15. Shouldn't the EA have exited this trade back when trendslope changed to long? You'll notice obviously that the short is still in place- of course which turned out to be a good thing, but still I'd like to understand the functionality and logic of the EA. Not sure what I'm missing- Thanks for any thoughts.

G-Man, the way I understand the code of the slope indicator is that it looks at the current price's position relative to the previous price.   
  
If current > previous Slope Up  
If current < previous Slope Down

  * Jan 29, 2008 6:33am  Jan 29, 2008 6:33am 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar43541_7.gif) Ronald Raygun](ronald*raygun)

  * Joined Jul 2007 | Status: 33 y/o Investor/Trader/Programmer | [5,016 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=43541)

Ok, the way the slope indicator works is that it checks its current MA value and the Previous MA value. If the current is greater than the previous, then the slope is up. If the current is less than the previous, then the slope is down.   
  
My EA works the same way.   
  
The exit however is a little funky. I set the EA to exit based on the highest TF's slope changing. Do you all want something else?  
  
As for your specific situation generalz, can you come up with a screenshot of any missed/misplaced trades by my EA?

  * [#238](/thread/post/1837164#post1837164 "Post Permalink")

  * Feb 6, 2008 12:29pm  Feb 6, 2008 12:29pm 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar43541_7.gif) Ronald Raygun](ronald*raygun)

  * Joined Jul 2007 | Status: 33 y/o Investor/Trader/Programmer | [5,016 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=43541)

Ok, color changing earlier? It's easier said than done. Let me explain.   
  
The original indicator posted at the beginning of the thread determined the slope in a very simple fashion.   
  
The slope is UP if the Current Value is greater than the Previous Value.   
The slope is DOWN if the Current Value is less than the Previous Value.  
  
Is there some other slope-determining metric that you propose we use? 

[0 ](javascript:void\(0\);) [0 ](javascript:void\(0\);)

> 
> Ignored

Let me try to make this clear for you.   
  
It is impossible to magically shift the charts back so you can enter the trade where you wanted to enter.   
  
  
Abnormalone has a point and thankfully, TrendSlopeV2 has the MAPeriod function built in. 

[0 ](javascript:void\(0\);) [0 ](javascript:void\(0\);)

  * [#242](/thread/post/1838535#post1838535 "Post Permalink")

  * Feb 7, 2008 3:18am  Feb 7, 2008 3:18am 

  * [ Peanutdude](peanutdude)

  * | Joined Dec 2007  | Status: Trader | [24 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=56960)

> [Quoting ele](/thread/post/1837141#post1837141 "View Quoted Post")
> 
> Disliked
> 
> Tks for your assistance.  
>  I downloaded the original EA,what I intended to update is that the color changing too late,we may get false signals. I found if make color changing more earlier. Such problems will be solved.  
>  So i need some programmers to make color changing period earlier.  
>    
>  Hope to get any comments from you all.  
>  Ele
> 
> Ignored

Actually you are wrong, having the color change earlier is trying to predict what the market will do, if we knew in advance what the market would do, we would not be here, we would already be retired living on a nice private island somewhere.  
  
There is no way to predict in advance if the trend is changing or not, you would get more false signals your way, than waiting and make sure the signals are valid.  
  
From what i've seen so far, most of the losing trades are when the higher TF has been in a trend for a while, and then you are looking for a reentry, when it could actually be nearing a trend change.  
  
That is just something that will happen, you have too look at total pips gained, against total pips lost in the long run. 

[0 ](javascript:void\(0\);) [0 ](javascript:void\(0\);)

If you are using TrendSlopeV2 you need to make sure that it has a Unique Magic Number from the other EAs that you're running. A magic number of 0 means that the EA will work on any open trade.

I don't mean for this to be a major issue it would just be nice to know how the indicator works so you can adjust for it at the turning points.

  * [#263](/thread/post/1847793#post1847793 "Post Permalink")

  * Feb 13, 2008 5:42am  Feb 13, 2008 5:42am 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar43541_7.gif) Ronald Raygun](ronald*raygun)

  * Joined Jul 2007 | Status: 33 y/o Investor/Trader/Programmer | [5,016 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=43541)

Ok, here is a new version of the EA.   
  
It exits based on whatever TF you choose. For example, the default is when the Base TF changes color, exit a trade.   
  
It can be set so that either the Base, Secondary, or Tertiary slope is used. 

Attached File(s)

![File Type: mq4](https://assets.faireconomy.media/images/attach/mq4.gif) [TrendSlopev3.mq4](/attachment/file/86013?d=1202848994) 10 KB | 2,048 downloads

  * [#266](/thread/post/1848299#post1848299 "Post Permalink")

  * Feb 13, 2008 1:05pm  Feb 13, 2008 1:05pm 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar43541_7.gif) Ronald Raygun](ronald*raygun)

  * Joined Jul 2007 | Status: 33 y/o Investor/Trader/Programmer | [5,016 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=43541)

Yes, just set the ExitOnPrimary variable to true, and the remaining others to false.   
  
That way, if the slope of the primary changes, then it will close the trade.

  * [#268](/thread/post/1848344#post1848344 "Post Permalink")

  * Feb 13, 2008 1:43pm  Feb 13, 2008 1:43pm 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar43541_7.gif) Ronald Raygun](ronald*raygun)

  * Joined Jul 2007 | Status: 33 y/o Investor/Trader/Programmer | [5,016 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=43541)

If you only want to use the BaseTF to determine when to enter, set all the variables for the TFs to the same as Base.  
  
For example, if I wanted to only use the basetf as my basis for entry.  
  
BaseTF = 60  
Secondary = 60  
Tertiary = 60

All of my EAs manage one trade at a time. So, there's nothing to worry about with regard to managing multiple trades. If you want multiple trades managed, then you need multiple EAs.

  * [#272](/thread/post/1855318#post1855318 "Post Permalink")

  * Feb 17, 2008 7:08pm  Feb 17, 2008 7:08pm 

  * [ Topgun](topgun)

  * | Joined Sep 2007  | Status: Trader | [123 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=49135)

I think there is an easier way than having 3 charts open...lets say you have or want 5min 15min and 60 min and a slope setting of 20, then simply add slope 3 times to a 5 min chart and have settings of 20, 60 (20 x 3 as a 15 min chart is 3x a 5 min chart) and 240 ( 20 x 12 as a 60 min chart is 5 x 12)  
then you have all 3 on one chart

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar57597_6.gif) timex83](timex83)

  * | Joined Jan 2008  | Status: Monopoly | [83 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=57597)

> [Quoting Ronald Raygun](/thread/post/1837164#post1837164 "View Quoted Post")
> 
> Disliked
> 
> Ok, color changing earlier? It's easier said than done. Let me explain.   
>    
>  The original indicator posted at the beginning of the thread determined the slope in a very simple fashion.   
>    
>  The slope is UP if the Current Value is greater than the Previous Value.   
>  The slope is DOWN if the Current Value is less than the Previous Value.  
>    
>  Is there some other slope-determining metric that you propose we use?
> 
> Ignored

What if u place this instead of using simple moving average to find the slope?  
  
int SlopeDirection(int TF, int SlopePeriod, int SlopeMethod, int SlopePrice)  
{  
int Trend =999;  
  
//calculate slope for daily  
double Buffer0 = iCustom(NULL, TF, "Slope Direction Line", SlopePeriod,SlopeMethod,SlopePrice, 0, 0);  
double Buffer1 = iCustom(NULL, TF, "Slope Direction Line", SlopePeriod,SlopeMethod,SlopePrice, 1, 0);  
  
if(Buffer0 == EMPTY_VALUE)  
Trend = 1; //short  
if(Buffer1 == EMPTY_VALUE)  
Trend = 2; //long  
  
if (Trend == 999 && IsTesting() == true)  
Print("Buffer0: " + Buffer0 + " | Buffer1: " + Buffer1);   
return (Trend);  
}

I just found this thread having been introduced to the Signal Line, aka Slope Direction Line, in the Imran Sait thread. (aka Hull MA?)  
  
I have tried and liked 'slope' methods already and I believe they benefit a lot from having the slope value shown on an indicator similar to fig1. This allows accept/reject levels for slope to be set on the indicator.  
(This is my attempt by placing a lagging MA on a momentum plot)  
  
I found an HMAangle indicator (attached) and various other 'angle' indicators but it doesn't produce the correct plot even adjusting its inputs. fig2. Also the all important current value doesn't plot properly in real time. fig3.  
Obviously a quick check is the price (or the Slope Direction Line) _turning points_ should align with _zero crosses_ on the indicator. (red vert lines in fig1 - nearly!)  
  
A line plot is preferable to a histogram plot.  
  
What I'm looking for is an indicator simply based on the value of the HMA slope.  
  
Can any MT4 expert help and code one or modify the one attached please?   
Maybe someone has one already?  
  
thanks  
rorieu

  * [#311](/thread/post/2361316#post2361316 "Post Permalink")

  * Nov 19, 2008 11:34pm  Nov 19, 2008 11:34pm 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar34376_4.gif) dod](dod)

  * | Joined Feb 2007  | Status: Trader | [90 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=34376)

I trade a variant of the Slope System, using four HMA indicators, one extra long term, one long term, one medium term, and the other short term. The numbers aren't that important, I find, so long as once established, they're never changed. I look for a trade when the extra long, long and medium term indicators are all pointing in the same direction but the short term indicater is pointing in the opposite direction. I then try and time a trade to coincide or even precede the short term line turning in the same direction as the other three lines. If I haven't entered by the time the short term line has turned, I skip the trade.  
  
What would help me a lot is an alarm that could send me an email (or better, an SMS) whenever the extra long, long and medium term lines are pointing in the same direction. This doesn't happen that often, and as I use 1 minute charts, I'd rather not have to sit around waiting; but second guessing when it's likely to happen, I often miss opportunities.   
  
Does anyone know if such an alarm is possible? 

All flesh is as grass

  * [#316](/thread/post/2369978#post2369978 "Post Permalink")

  * Nov 23, 2008 6:26pm  Nov 23, 2008 6:26pm 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar34376_4.gif) dod](dod)

  * | Joined Feb 2007  | Status: Trader | [90 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=34376)

It's still a 'work in progress'. For example, let's say you want to trade a particular timeframe. You put the 80HMA, as suggested by EMATrader on it, and then you add an 80HMA from two higher time frames. If you trade 15 min then you would add 240HMA (80x4 because there are 4 fifteen minutes in an hour) and 640HMA (80x8 periods of fifteen minutes in four hours). Then, I would add a shorter HMA, say a 15 or 20, also.  
  
Only take trades when the three bigger HMAs are running together; but rather than wait for the smaller HMA to run with them too, try and trade the break of that HMA, just before it turns.  
  
I actually do this on 1 min charts, slightly differently, with a 1200HMA, 300HMA, 75HMA, and 15HMA. I'm not sure how I figured out these numbers!  
  
After the 1200HMA turns (this is also a 1 hour 20HMA turn: 20x60=1200) I wait for the 75HMA to turn against the 1200HMA and then (so long as the 75 is above the 1200 for longs and below the 1200 for shorts, I enter when price breaks the 75HMA line. The break is the key - I sometimes wait for it to poke through, drop back, and go through again ... this is subjective!  
  
The 15HMA and 300HMA are redundant in this model; but the same principle applies to turns in the 300 and breaks of the 15.  
  
  
  
That might give you some idea. 

All flesh is as grass

  * [#318](/thread/post/2371619#post2371619 "Post Permalink")

  * Nov 24, 2008 6:43pm  Nov 24, 2008 6:43pm 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar34376_4.gif) dod](dod)

  * | Joined Feb 2007  | Status: Trader | [90 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=34376)

Does it work? Not without trade selection, no!   
  
Here are a couple of charts. One shows the 1200, 300, 75, and 15. The other shows the 1200 and 75, with nearby HMAs to make ribbons. At present, using this approach, I trade the first cross of the 75 after the first 1200 turn during the London market (this shows as the green line below). I've put an arrow indicating the trade. One trade a day, that's all.  
  
There's loads of different ways you could trade this, though, like the 15 cross after the 300 turn. For me, the crux is going against the smaller HMA, entering when price makes its move, rather than with the HMA, by which time the move is often over.  
  
This morning's trade was no great shakes, though.  
  
As I said, a work in progress.

  * [#322](/thread/post/2570894#post2570894 "Post Permalink")

  * Mar 1, 2009 9:14am  Mar 1, 2009 9:14am 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar92149_1.gif) chamane](chamane)

  * Joined Jan 2009 | Status: Trader | [1,987 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=92149)

Hi Baz,  
  
Thanks for the link. Have you tried that system yourself? I have but I got discouraged after a couple of losses. Maybe I should keep trying. It would be nice to show your track records if you happen to have one.  
  
Regarding the possibility of combining this system with the Slope, I don't know if I would be able to interpret the chart correctly. I have the feeling that there would be too much indicators telling the same thing. AO, AC (I think) and Stochastic are based on moving averages and so is HMA (or the Slope) obviously.  
  
I have tried many systems so far and the approach I prefer up to now is the multiple timeframe approach because I understand what is going on (although I would love to predict it 100%). It's a matter of doubling the retracement and momentum at different scales. The nice thing there is to it is that you can use the indicator you want. I guess you should know that...![](https://resources.faireconomy.media/images/emojis/64/1f61e.png?v=15.1)  
  
Anyway, I am trying to make a setup of the Slope system for scalping 5min charts (see picture) wich is what I prefer because the risks are smaller and you can still make over 100 pips per day wich is my goal using. It would use the HMAs and PSAR. My rules are buy or sell when HMAs, PSAR and the last closed candle are in agreement.  
  
I don't have much experience in money management, that is what I am working on right now. I would set initial stop loss on the last PSAR dot and manually move the stop to each subsequent dot, and to the breakeven + 10 pips whenever possible (as quick as possible). Afterwards, move the stop to every slice of 25 pips if situation allows it. Also, I think I would entry once again at every retracement of PSAR if HMAs are still in agreement. The important thing would be to take advantage of long movements so to cut down losses as much and as soon as possible.  
  
Chamane

Thanks. It's already bookmarked. I am starting this week with my settings and will see how it works. I am using HMA34, HMA65 and HMA125 to start off. I thought lower periods for the current timeframe will produce to many whipsaws, but I will still keep an eye on that. Actually, I use HMA13 for timeframes 5 times (HMA65) and 25 times (HMA125) higher than the current. They're basic Fibonacci numbers (13 and 34). It's just an idea to start. I will adjust with first results and according to pairs.  
  
Chamane

  * Mar 16, 2009 10:38am  Mar 16, 2009 10:38am 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar24119_7.gif) tcmm](tcmm)

  * | Commercial User  | Joined Nov 2006 | [1,023 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=24119)

OK Guys Try This.  
-Open a Daily Chart ie: GBP/JPY  
-Add the Slope Line Indicator to Chart and in the Inputs Set at 12-3-0.  
-Add another Slope Line Indicator and in the Inputs Set at 80-3-0.  
-The 80 Slope Line Shows you the Trend  
-The 12 Slope Line Shows you the Retracements.  
-Now when the Retracement comes to a end, which is the 12 Slope line go in the trade when both the 80 and 12 are going the same Direction and Exit when the 12 changes colour. See Chart below.  
I went in this one at 136.98 at 6.04 EST. 

Attached Image (click to enlarge)

[![Click to Enlarge

If you want you can trade off a timeframe but always make sure you check 2 lower frames IE: -Monthly is Trade Chart-Check Weekly and Daily.Make sure Slopes are same coluor.  
Weekly is Trade Chart-Check Daily and 4Hour  
Daily is trade Chart-Check 4Hour and 1 hour  
And so on.  
But the method is better on Daily less time on computer and more steady pips

Maybe was someone else wtih the same name.  
  
1) Open a 1hr and a 15min. charts  
2) Put a 200ma on the charts  
3) Set and put a _MACD 12-20-9_ Crossed same direction as 200ma both charts  
4) Stoch at 8-3-3 Just to show Overbought and Oversold only  
5) Pivots to guide you  
6) 5ma close and 8ma open When they cross  
7) When both charts have 200ma same trend and MACD cross the same and the 5 and 8 cross Buy the dips in an uptrend,  
and sell the rallies in a downtrend.  
  
<http://www.forexfactory.com/showthread.php?t=74608>

On these trades the CHF/JPY I went in late should of went in at 83.45 when the slopes were the same colour up and you can cofirm with 4hr and 1hr that they are the same colour.  
Keep in mind too that when the 80 slope shows main trend and the 12 slope retraces and then when the 12 slope is the same colour its good to go in.   
  
SELL THE RALLIES IN A DOWNTREND  
BUY THE DIPS IN A UPTREND

> [Quoting Ronald Raygun](/thread/post/1849814#post1849814 "View Quoted Post")
> 
> Disliked

> All of my EAs manage one trade at a time. So, there's nothing to worry about with regard to managing multiple trades. If you want multiple trades managed, then you need multiple EAs.

Hi Ronald,  
  
1\. You mentioned that V1 was a complete stop and reverse EA. Does this applies to V3?  
  
2\. If i want the EA to buy or sell on M15 (base on H1), are my settings correct as follows:  
attach the EA to M15 chart  
EachTickMode=False  
Base = 60  
Secondary = 30  
Tertiary = 15  
ExitOnPrimary = True  
ExitOnSecondary = True  
ExitOnTertiary = True  
My aim is to have multiple open and close orders in M15 in compliance with H1  
  
3\. Current stop loss is a fixed stop loss system. Do you think you are able to come out with a version where you can select the mode of stop loss as follows:  
Fixed Stop Loss (currently on EA)  
Or  
For Sell, Stop Loss at last Swing High + 1pip + Spread  
For Buy, Stop Loss at last Swing Low - 1 pip  
Both subject to parameter set in Fixed Stop Loss  
  
Thanks.  
![](https://resources.faireconomy.media/images/emojis/64/1f60a.png?v=15.1)

  Victor V

Lenoxer,  
Tested for 3 months on a demo account with great results.  
On my live account I am still dealing with decent stop loss. In other words I have to controll emotions and fear.  
  
I some occasions I had to set my stop loss to 200-250 pips. This is too much for my coronaries.  
Right now I exit (if necessary) at 80-100 pips and reenter when the trend goes again in my favour. It usually does.   
  
In general I think is a very good system. I will keep it on my live account.  
I only added a MTF stoch indicator + Slope set at 12 to see crosses with Slope 80.

Hi Joseph,  
  
I am using this system for position as well as swing trades. mainly on the euro and once in a while when the euro and the yen is heading in the same direction, I will trade the euro yen. I don't like the pound, even though it is mostly trending I find that placing the stop at the last significant price does not allow me to enter with a decent sized position. As far as money management is conscerned you have to first get to know the system you are trading as if it is your own. Doing backtesting with the MTF Russian HMA indicator will help a lot. If you don't know the system you are trading then even risking 1% is to much, aka gambling. You really have to make some effort and make this system your own, then risking even 10% at a time won't be to much.  
  
Hope this helps,  
  
Regards  
  
Ben.

  * [ racerdude777](racerdude777)

  * | Joined Feb 2010  | Status: Trader | [2 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=133768)

If you want to be more aggressive on the entry you can wait until the value shown for the slope under the data section on the left hand side of the screen is the same on the close for the previous two bars. This indicates the slope is leveling off, meaning a turn around is coming.   
  
This tends to work on the mid time frames (M30, H1, H4) best

> 
> Ignored

I don't see any possible way for this system or an ea of this system to work in a static context. In range, just like all other systems, it will take back the pips because by the time the slope flips, you will have already taken a beating for the oh sh$t bar (the trend breaker).  
  
One filter you may consider is trading this when the longer term slopes are already trending and the shortest term has just flipped. If the long term slope signal is the last to flip, you're going to lose pips usually.  
  
Charlie, my advice would be to try to dissect a system, find out why it works, what scenarios are giving back money and why. You'll drive yourself to the brink of insanity, but the reward will be successful trading.  
  
Ask James16, ask Nial fuller, ask Mr. Charts from T2W, ask Tro, any of the trading rockstars that are nice enough to still post on boards to help aspiring traders. All of these guys have systems but it's their hard work and knowledge of trading that makes them able to trade successfully.   
  
They all teach that it takes more than just a system and it is absolutely right. Slope lines alone aren't a holy grail. But they can be, if you find a unique way to use them that fits your style.

Something I have been working on for awhile as the Williams Wise 1 entry sucks

SDL 300

Alligator  
Fractals  
Wiseman 2

SDL 800

Alligator  
Fractals  
Wiseman 2

SDL 800  
Alligator  
Fractals  
Wiseman 2  
**M30**  
SDL 800  
Alligator  
Fractals  
Wiseman 2

  * [#419](/thread/post/4044625#post4044625 "Post Permalink")

  * Sep 24, 2010 3:44am  Sep 24, 2010 3:44am 

  * [ BlueBull](bluebull)

  * | Joined Jun 2007  | Status: Trader | [65 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=41944)

"Look, for example, at this elegant little experiment. A rat was put in a T-shaped maze with a few morsels of food placed on either the far right or left side of the enclosure. The placement of the food is randomly determined, but the dice is rigged: over the long run, the food was placed on the left side sixty per cent of the time. How did the rat respond? It quickly realized that the left side was more rewarding. **As a result, it always went to the left, which resulted in a sixty percent success rate. The rat didn't strive for perfection.** It didn't search for a Unified Theory of the T-shaped maze, or try to decipher the disorder. Instead, it accepted the inherent uncertainty of the reward and learned to settle for the best possible alternative.   
  
The experiment was then repeated with Yale undergraduates. Unlike the rat, their swollen brains stubbornly searched for the elusive pattern that determined the placement of the reward. They made predictions and then tried to learn from their prediction errors. The problem was that there was nothing to predict: the randomness was real. Because the students refused to settle for a 60 percent success rate, they ended up with a 52 percent success rate. **Although most of the students were convinced they were making progress towards identifying the underlying algorithm, they were actually being outsmarted by a rat**." - P64 _**"HOW WE DECIDE"**_  
  
  
What I realized was all conventional trading wisdom is "wrong".  
  
I have distilled trading into the following:  
  
**ALL YOU NEED TO KNOW ABOUT TRADING**

  1. Price either goes up or down.
  2. No one knows what will happen next.
  3. Keep losses small and let winners run.
  4. POSITION SIZE = RISK / STOP LOSS
  5. The reason you entered has no bearing on the outcome of your trade.
  6. You can control the size of your loss (skill) but you can't control the size of your win (luck).
  7. You need to know when to pick up your chips and cash them in. 

Expectancy = (Probability of Win * Average Win) - (Probability of Loss * Average Loss)   
You can not control the probabilities of wining or losing.  
You can not control your average win size.  
The only part of the equation of the equation that you can control is your average loss size.  
  
  
  
_**THE ILLUSION OF CONTROL**_  
  
  
_"Individuals appear hard-wired to overattribute success to skill, and to underestimate the role of chance, when both are in fact present."_  
  
[Langer, E. J., The Illusion of Control, Journal of Personality and  
Social Psychology 32 (2), 311-328 (1975)]  
  
_**FINANCIAL MANAGEMENT**_  
  
  
_"After a full cycle of rise and fall after which stocks were valued just where they were at the start, all his clients lost money (Don Guyon, 1909).  
  
Many academic works suggest that most managers underperform "buy-and-hold" strategy; persistence of winners is very rare, etc.  
  
Most funds consistently fail to overperform random strategies (dart throwing)."_   
  
  
**OVER-OPTIMIZATION**  
  
**Rats beat humans in simple games**  
  
**People makes STORIES!**  
  
_"Normal people have an "interpreter" in their left brain that takes all the random, contradictory details of whatever they are doing or remembering at the moment, and smoothes everything in one coherent story. If there are details that do not fit, they are edited out or revised!"_  
  
(T. Grandin and C. Johnson, Animals in translation (Scribner,  
New York, 2005)  
  
  
[PDF here](http://www.er.ethz.ch/presentations/Illusion_of_control_Zurich_CCSS-conf19Aug08.pdf)  
  
**The rat will beat you if you do not understand this.**

  * [#430](/thread/post/4734226#post4734226 "Post Permalink")

  * Jun 29, 2011 6:04am  Jun 29, 2011 6:04am 

  * [ guitarRabbi](guitarrabbi)

  * | Joined May 2011  | Status: Trader | [3 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=177895)

I noticed a pattern for entry to get in to the slope system.When the bar crosses over the moving average either up or down and the bar is still the same color,meaning, if the trend is down and the bar crosses over above the moving average, that is a sign that the trend could change.So if you check the one hour chart and 30 min chart and they also concur that the trend has changed, I am suggesting that even though the bar still shows the trend is up, it could be time to trade the other way.

Sasha -- I have used this system with good, but inconsistent results on lower time frames.  
  
I built an EA that looked at 1 HR, 30 min and 15 min time frames and traded when 80 EMA aligned on all three time frames.  
  
I was up about 44% over 3-4 months and then I increased my lot size. Then I lost about 9 trades in a row, and I've been down ever since. Maybe just unlucky, or maybe the system is only good no higher TF.

  * Jul 26, 2020 10:17pm  Jul 26, 2020 10:17pm 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar183315_23.gif) DrDave](drdave)

  * | Membership Revoked  | Joined Jun 2011 | [9,885 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=183315)

The basic idea presented in this thread is a very good one. However, there are unseen problems with it as presented because of the limited selection of time frames. If you switch to a charting application that has custom time frames of any period that you choose, then you can make so further analyses with other TFs to find the ones that work the best together. In addition, it may be worth your time to experiment with the Trend Slope settings.  
  
And, many have said that they had a lot of losses during ranging periods. Did you think to try a volatility filter, like maybe ATR???   
  
And too many people just blindly went with the rules laid out by the OP but never considered money management. DUH! Maybe if you take the idea that was presented and DEVELOP AROUND THAT CORE an actual TRADING SYSTEM, you would finally have consistent green pips every month.  
  
Even with the limitations of using MT4, you can still make money with this. 

To free Gazans of Hamas, use whatever it takes.

The tricks are to find the right trading period, the right setting and to avoid flat markets when trading with the slope direction line. This chart shows M15 with slope direction line period 25. I don't close my trade when the market goes flat instead I wait for a clear direction change to close the trade or let it continue. Please note the flat period.
